  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_05a10e93-e9b6-4ad3-a77e-475c31bde32a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10064754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10442045219534753557"><b>
  <u>Creepy fun reading!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>LAUGHING WHILE CREEPING OUT!</u>
</b><br/><br/>This is a great novel, only that curiously when I bought this book, I bought also, another novel by Dean Koontz titled "Life Expectancy" (you can see my review of that book here: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10064726' rel='nofollow noopener'>Life Expectancy</a> . <br/><br/>I comment this, since I found both novels quite similar.<br/><br/>Not exactly the general story and developing but the mood of the storyline.<br/><br/>I totally adored <i>Life Expectancy</i> and I jumped right after that book to read this one and I was like "Mmh, I'm feeling</span>
  <span id="freeText10442045219534753557" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Creepy fun reading!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>LAUGHING WHILE CREEPING OUT!</u>
</b><br /><br />This is a great novel, only that curiously when I bought this book, I bought also, another novel by Dean Koontz titled "Life Expectancy" (you can see my review of that book here: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10064726" rel="nofollow noopener">Life Expectancy</a> . <br /><br />I comment this, since I found both novels quite similar.<br /><br />Not exactly the general story and developing but the mood of the storyline.<br /><br />I totally adored <i>Life Expectancy</i> and I jumped right after that book to read this one and I was like "Mmh, I'm feeling like deja vú".<br /><br />But don't get me wrong, the stories are totally different but I think that since before of these two books, I hadn't read a Dean Koontz book with such many humor elements, usually you find characters quite likable and some amusing moments where you smile, but so far, my Koont experience was strictly of creepy horror, not creepy fun.<br /><br />And I don't tell this as something bad, since I think that's kinda expected to do standard horror, but crafting stories with clear horror intention, but with such rich funny sense, it's quite cool.<br /><br />Even recently, you find a lot of this in movies and TV series, but at least me, back in 2007, it wasn't something so usual.<br /><br />But I totally embrace it.<br /><br />So, initially, I thought that <i>Life Expectancy</i> was like unique on that angle, but right after I read that one, I found here, in <i>Ticktock</i>, another horror book with rich humor elements.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THOSE WONDERFUL WOMEN</u>
</b><br /><br />Another thing that I found quite similar is the female companion character of the main protagonist.<br /><br />On both books, the main protagonist finds a spectacular female character with great personality.<br /><br />So, while I loved both characters in each novel, it didn't help to my "deja vú" feeling.<br /><br />I know that Dean Koontz re-use a lot of elements, like smart dogs, protagonists who like to read and/or are writers, over-detailed towns, etc... and I love his work for all that. <br /><br />As I say, "Tick Tock" is a wonderful horror story with a great humorous ambiance, quite entertaining and a really page-turner. <br /><br />In fact I read it quite quickly. So, I still recommend it a lot. Just try to read this book, <i>Ticktock</i> and <i>Life Expectancy</i> with some time in between of each of them.<br /><br />Quite advisable, if you read something else, of a different genre, in between.<br /><br />I'm sure that you'll enjoy both books!!!<br /><br />Have creepy fun!!!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10442045219534753557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1589834401" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17137210305852529020">Tommy Phan buys a new Corvette and, pleased with his purchase, he cruises around for awhile in his dream car. After he gets home the doorbell at the front of his house rings. When he answers the door no one is there, but someone has left a strange cloth doll with a note attached to it on his doorstep.   <span id="freeText17137210305852529020" style="display:none">Tommy Phan buys a new Corvette and, pleased with his purchase, he cruises around for awhile in his dream car. After he gets home the doorbell at the front of his house rings. When he answers the door no one is there, but someone has left a strange cloth doll with a note attached to it on his doorstep. After bringing the doll into his house Tommy lives to regret it.<br /><br />This was a fast-paced, sometimes funny, and really strange read. It was sort of a horror-comedy. I liked Tommy. I enjoyed his inner thoughts (which were mostly hilarious---but I don't know if they were supposed to be) as he dealt with his "doll" suddenly coming to life. The girl Tommy eventually befriends, Del Payne, was a friendly, gutsy, and totally kooky girl. Some people who read this book will like her, some people will find her annoying. Her character was a bit "out there", weird---she was sort of an oddball. I did like her cute dog Scootie. The doll/demon/creature gave this book some spooky moments and Tommy's obstinate Vietnamese mother was funny at times. <br /><br />An offbeat, silly, fun read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17137210305852529020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_153631517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153631517" />
    <a title="Robyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5106028-robyn"><img alt="Robyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441402727p2/5106028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153631517?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robyn" href="/user/show/5106028-robyn">Robyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5106028-robyn?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153631517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11747468065683654527">What a mess. This book is just all over the place. From the nonsensical story line, to the overly goofy characters, Everything in this book can't seem to make up it's mind about what to be. It's not scary enough to be a horror novel, and the strangeness and bad puns want to make it a comedy, but it isn't very funny. I really feel as though the major plot points were chosen at random, perhaps through the "pull some words out of a hat and make a story about them" method. You can make a good story </span>
  <span id="freeText11747468065683654527" style="display:none">What a mess. This book is just all over the place. From the nonsensical story line, to the overly goofy characters, Everything in this book can't seem to make up it's mind about what to be. It's not scary enough to be a horror novel, and the strangeness and bad puns want to make it a comedy, but it isn't very funny. I really feel as though the major plot points were chosen at random, perhaps through the "pull some words out of a hat and make a story about them" method. You can make a good story that way, but if you do, it's because you have used a lot of care and patience plotting out where these disparate elements come together. In this case, you end up with a jumbled mess, with new ideas introduced at random and the most out of nowhere ending I've ever read. When I finished this, I wanted to walk up to Dean Koontz, wave the book in his face and ask "What the heck was that all about?"</span>
  <a data-text-id="11747468065683654527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1192063461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192063461" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532221628p2/23841736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192063461?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780739334287" href="/book/show/13133376-ticktock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192063461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9404585016196642489">I wasn't particularly crazy about this the first time I read it. It's an odd book with some slightly bizarre humor. I knew that he wrote this because the other books he was writing got too intense but I was intrigued by the afterword. Apparently his goal with this was to combine a supernatural thriller with screwball comedy. This explains soooo much.<br/><br/>This book is the sole reason that I always hesitate over bringing an unknown package into the house, even though I read it over 15 years ago.<br/><br/>Tommy P</span>
  <span id="freeText9404585016196642489" style="display:none">I wasn't particularly crazy about this the first time I read it. It's an odd book with some slightly bizarre humor. I knew that he wrote this because the other books he was writing got too intense but I was intrigued by the afterword. Apparently his goal with this was to combine a supernatural thriller with screwball comedy. This explains soooo much.<br /><br />This book is the sole reason that I always hesitate over bringing an unknown package into the house, even though I read it over 15 years ago.<br /><br />Tommy Phan is a Vietnamese-American who wants nothing more than to be as American as possible, to the great dismay of his mother. At the start of the book he's just bought a Corvette and he's talking to his mother on his car phone. She berates him for being a bad son and tries to force him into coming over for dinner. She complains about his detective character in the book that he's just sold and accuses him of eating too many cheeseburgers and chasing blondes. He manages to evade going over for dinner and in a fit of rebellion he orders <i>two</i> cheeseburgers at a local diner.<br /><br />Later that night Tommy hears someone on his porch and goes to check it out. He finds a gingerbread shaped rag doll on his porch and <i>he brings it in the house</i>. Hence my paranoia because the thing comes to life and then spends the rest of the night trying to kill him, which it must do before dawn. Ticktock.<br /><br />It's a fun book but it's not one that I can get deeply attached to. It's perfect for whiling the day away with a few laughs.<br /><br />However, whatever you do, <i>do not use the audio!!!</i> It was beyond atrocious! The narrator was the same guy that I loved so much in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/359375.Night_Watch__Watch___1_" title="Night Watch (Watch, #1) by Sergei Lukyanenko" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Watch</a>, but good god! It turns out that where, to my ear at least, his Russian accent is quite good, he totally freaking sucks at Vietnamese. Seriously. He sounded like an American with a mouth full of marbles trying for a Chinese accent and calling it Vietnamese. Truly. Freaking. Terrible. It's a bit difficult to get truly absorbed in a book that sounds like a slushy version of Joy Luck Club. Did I mention it was <i>absolutely awful</i>? To top it off, there's a great deal of banter that is of the screwball comedy variety. But instead of deadpan comments that show that Del knows more about what's going on than Tommy, the narrator constantly adds inflection that makes it flirtatious or smug or <i>whatever</i>. Anything but straight and perfectly serious.<br /><br />So... read this when you need a laugh but nothing deep. And don't.... Oh, am I repeating myself?<br /><br />And because the quote made me laugh:<br /><br /><i>"You steal my son," said Mother Phan.<br /> "No," Del said, "I stole a Honda and later a Ferrari, and then we borrowed the Peterbilt that the demon stole, but I didn't steal your son."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9404585016196642489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123717609" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/175164-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1183811586p2/175164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123717609?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/175164-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780753151587" href="/book/show/2224629.Tick_Tock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/175164-andrew?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123717609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer370053489352000964">This book offends me greatly. I was offended at the first 30 pages of foreigner stereotypes (give a Vietnamese mother a food obsession, over-protectedness and an inability to form predicates despite otherwise idiomatic English and you get Koontz' ridiculously pathetic attempt at being "diverse.") Hideous!<br/><br/>As horror it's also pathetic. Too much happens too soon. There's no build-up or tension. An inane monster (sort of) terrorizes two idiots when they're not engaged in the most banal dialogue ever</span>
  <span id="freeText370053489352000964" style="display:none">This book offends me greatly. I was offended at the first 30 pages of foreigner stereotypes (give a Vietnamese mother a food obsession, over-protectedness and an inability to form predicates despite otherwise idiomatic English and you get Koontz' ridiculously pathetic attempt at being "diverse.") Hideous!<br /><br />As horror it's also pathetic. Too much happens too soon. There's no build-up or tension. An inane monster (sort of) terrorizes two idiots when they're not engaged in the most banal dialogue ever. I was praying the protagonists would get mauled. Jane Austen wrote scarier novels.<br /><br />Honestly, this is one of the worst books I've ever read. Like a b-movie I was just fascinated by how increasingly dumber and dumber the plot twists got and how screwball the characters were. When I finished the book I said a prayer for all the trees that died to make this literary turd.</span>
  <a data-text-id="370053489352000964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1107436194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1107436194" />
    <a title="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl"><img alt="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320959271p2/2454496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1107436194?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" href="/user/show/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl">Dustin Crazy little brown owl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781568652870" href="/book/show/3320375-ticktock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=dogs">dogs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1107436194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6725902352354953468">This is a fun trip into Vietnamese and American Cultures with a good deal of the mystical and magical. Amid the silliness, there is wisdom. Here is a novel about traditions and learning to see the world in new awareness. <br/><br/>Favorite Passages:<br/><i> What a drag it was to be limited by reality. Tommy sighed and wished that he could step magically through the pages of his own books . . .<br/>________<br/><br/>Again Tommy had the queer sensation that he was riding the bobsled of fate, rocketing down a luge chute toward som</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6725902352354953468" style="display:none">This is a fun trip into Vietnamese and American Cultures with a good deal of the mystical and magical. Amid the silliness, there is wisdom. Here is a novel about traditions and learning to see the world in new awareness. <br /><br />Favorite Passages:<br /><i> What a drag it was to be limited by reality. Tommy sighed and wished that he could step magically through the pages of his own books . . .<br />________<br /><br />Again Tommy had the queer sensation that he was riding the bobsled of fate, rocketing down a luge chute toward some destiny he could not begin to understand. <br />________<br /><br />"Are you a New Age type or something - channel spirits, heal yourself with crystals?"<br />"No. I merely said reality is perception."<br />"Sounds New Age," he said, returning to watch her finish her own task.<br />"Well, it's not. I'll explain someday when we have more time."<br />"Meanwhile," he said, "I'll wander aimlessly in the wilderness of my ignorance."<br />_______<br /><br />"Relax, Tommy. There's always enough time if you think there is."<br />"What's that mean?"<br />"Whatever you expect is what will be, so simply change your expectations."<br />"I don't know what that means, either."<br />"It means what it means," she said, enigmatic once more. <br />_______<br /><br />He went to have a closer look, and discovered that the beautiful grain was like rippled ribbons that appeared to undulate as he shifted his head from one side to the other. <br />_______<br /><br />Her eccentricities and her habit of peppering her conversation with cryptic babble and non sequiturs had convinced him that she had a few screws loose in the cranium, but now he suspected that the worst mistake he could make with her would be to write her off as a flake. There were depths to her that he was only beginning to perceive - and swimming in those depths were some strange fish that would surprise him more than anything that he had seen to date. <br /><br />He recalled another fragment of their conversation, and it seemed to have new import: Reality is perception. Perceptions change. Reality is fluid. So if by "reality" you mean reliably tangible objects and immutable events, then there no such thing . . . . I'll explain someday when we have more time.<br /><br />He sensed that every screwball statement she made was not, in fact, half as screwball as it seemed. Even in her most airheaded statements, an elusive truth was lurking. If he could just step back from her, put aside the conception of her that he had already formed, he would see her entirely differently form the way that he saw her now. He thought of those drawings by M. C. Escher, which played with perspective and with the viewer's expectations, so a scene might appear to be only a drift of lazily falling leaves until, suddenly, one saw it anew as a school of fast-swimming fish. Within the first picture was hidden another. Within Del Payne was hidden a different person - someone with a secret - who was cloaked by the ditsy image that she projected.<br /><br />The satori, tidal wave of revelation, loomed, loomed, loomed - and then began to recede without bringing him understanding. He had strained too hard. Sometimes enlightenment came only when it wasn't sought or welcomed.<br />_______<br /><br />Trying to get the discussion back on track, he said, "Are you really an artist?"<br />Sorting through the other coats in the closet, she said, "Is any of us really anything?"<br />Exasperated with Del's preference for speaking in cryptograms, Tommy indulged in one himself: "We're anything in the sense that we are everything."<br />"You've finally said something sensible."<br />_______<br /><br />Although no thunder or lightning had disturbed the night for hours, cataracts still crashed down from the riven sky.<br /><br />The queen palms hung limp, drizzling from the tip of every blade of every frond. Under the merciless lash of the rain, the lush ferns drooped almost to the point of humble prostration, their lacy pinnae glimmering with thousands upon thousands of droplets that, in the low landscape lighting, appeared to be incrustations of jewels. <br /><br />Scootie led the way, padding through the shallow puddles in the courtyard. In the quartzite paving, specks of mica glinted around the dog's splashing paws, almost as if his claws were striking sparks from the stone. That phantom fire marked his path along the walkway beside the house as well.<br /><br />The Art Deco panels of copper were cold against Tommy's hand as he pushed open the gate to the street. The hinges rasped like small whispering voices.<br />________<br /><br />"Obviously, they were marked for an unnatural extraction."<br />"Extraction?"<br />"From this world. If the thing in the fat man hadn't gotten them, then they would have been taken in some other unusual way. Like spontaneous combustion. Or an encounter with a lycanthrope."<br />"Lycanthrope? Werewolf?" He wasn't able to deal with her weirdness just now, so he changed the subject.<br />_______<br /><br />"What if I told you there are a few nights when I've had missing hours, blank spots, where I just seem to have blacked out, gone into a fugue state or something. All abductees report these missing hours, these holes in their memories where their abduction experiences have been erased or suppressed."<br />_______<br /><br />"What about ghosts?" he asked.<br />"What about them?"<br />"Do you believe in ghosts?"<br />"I've even met a few," she said brightly<br />"What about the healing power of crystals?"<br />She shook her head. "They can't heal, but they can focus your psychic power."<br />"Out-of-body experiences?"<br />"I'm sure it can be done, but I like my body too much to want to leave it even for a short time."<br />"Remote viewing?"<br />"That's easy. Pick a town."<br />_______<br /><br />"Everything is more than it seems, but nothing is as mysterious as it appears to be."<br />_______<br /><br />"He's just not prepared for this. He doesn't watch The X-Files."<br />"You not watch X-Files?" Mrs. Dai asked, astonished. <br />Shaking her head with dismay, Mother Phan said, "Probably watch junk detective show instead of good educational program."<br />_______<br /><br />"Negative thinking disturbs the fabric of the cosmos."<br />_______<br /><br />"This is reality, tofu man, because reality is what we carry in our hearts, and my heart is full of beauty just for you."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6725902352354953468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_129251542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129251542" />
    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129251542?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129251542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15077065312173849530">This review is for the abridged audiobook version. I keep meaning to get around to reading the entire book but something else always grabs my attention and the narrator read this book with such glee that I'm afraid I'd be disappointed. <br/><br/>Tommy Phan has just about everything he ever dreamed of; a successful career as a novelist, a brand new Corvette, and all the trappings that money can buy. His life would be perfect if only his Mother would stop making him feel guilty for forgetting his Vietnamese</span>
  <span id="freeText15077065312173849530" style="display:none">This review is for the abridged audiobook version. I keep meaning to get around to reading the entire book but something else always grabs my attention and the narrator read this book with such glee that I'm afraid I'd be disappointed. <br /><br />Tommy Phan has just about everything he ever dreamed of; a successful career as a novelist, a brand new Corvette, and all the trappings that money can buy. His life would be perfect if only his Mother would stop making him feel guilty for forgetting his Vietnamese roots.<br /><br />When Tommy returns home one night, after a particularly bad nagging phone call from Mom, he finds an innocent rag doll lying on his doorstep and brings it in for a closer inspection. This is when things start getting really weird. In no time at all Tommy, an eccentric woman who saves his butt, and her chocolate lab whose favorite toy is a farting hot-dog, are running for their lives from the devil's spawn. They have until dawn to outrun the demon.<br /><br />I really have to read the unabridged version of this book. I hate knowing I missed even one hilarious word. Unlike Koontz's most recent releases that were sometimes painfully dark, twisted and so intense I couldn't read them alone TICK TOCK is a more of a screwball comedy that reminded me of some of my favorite campy B horror flicks. I had visions of PUPPETMASTER &amp; NIGHT OF THE LIVING DEAD while reading and was reminded of my favorite kind of B movie demon: The beast that wouldn't die. This is not a criticism. There is nothing like a good campy B horror movie!<br /><br />Koontz creates the most likable off the wall characters: the guilt ridden down to earth Tommy Phan (I don't know anyone who hasn't experienced the "guilt" phone call), Deliverance Payne who continually surprised me with her strangeness, Scootie the face licker, and Tommy's Mom who has some of the most hilarious lines in the book. Which brings me to the dialogue - some of the funniest I've ever read. Too often humor can seem forced or stilted but never in this book. The characters were so kooky the wild dialogue flowed naturally. Some of my favorite scenes weren't the suspenseful chases or the gore filled shoot-outs but the bantering and bickering between the characters. TICK TOCK has a little bit of several of my favorite genres: horror, comedy, suspense, and a good old fashioned romance.<br /><br />I found there were a few unexplained plot points in the abridged version I read and I'm hoping they will be cleared up when I read the full version or maybe I'll just hope for a sequel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15077065312173849530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2521430094692370618" style="display:none">This book is about a man named Tommy who lives in California. One night he gets a doll that shows up on his door step. Then out of no where it comes alive and is on a mission to kill Tommy. Now, Tommy is running for his life meeting new people and trying to figure out why this thing is trying to kill him.<br />This book kept me reading because I wanted to know what would happen to Tommy and if he would survive the evil doll trying to kill him. I tryed to predict the ending, but predicting is a 50/50 chance because he could live or he could die. Also, as the book when on and he met new people he figured more and more things out about the doll that later helped him figure out how to defeat the enourmous evil doll.<br />My favorite character in this book had to be the doll because it was really funny with things that it did and it made me laugh a lot. In the book every character was funny and none of them i didnt like. So, i dont really have a least favorite character.<br />This book captivated my attention a lot, but the part that kept me captivated the most was when the doll first showed up on his doorstep and when he brought it in the house it would move. It captivated me because i wanted to know what was with the doll and what was going to happen to it and how it would effect Tommy. Reading this book made me feel really tense because when Tommy was running for his life sometimes the doll would get really close to getting him. I didnt want Tommy to die because then the ending would probably be really stupid.<br />I would recommend this book to anyone who likes horror books that are funny and really entertaining. Also, to people who dont mind a lot of suspense. Dean Koontz wrote this book to entertain people and who ever reads the book. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2462567608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16652678196420518064">Not going to lie, when I first read this years ago I actually loved it. I see the weaknesses now in the re-read though and gave this four stars. Also there is a dog and I just maybe sighed so hard I caused my poor cat's fur to ruffle. Aside: Not my fault she likes to get close when I am reading. Tick Tock actually shows that Koontz has a sense of humor. There are parts of this that are funny though when you find out the why behind this mess you are going to shake your head. <br/><br/>"Tick Tock" has Tommy</span>
  <span id="freeText16652678196420518064" style="display:none">Not going to lie, when I first read this years ago I actually loved it. I see the weaknesses now in the re-read though and gave this four stars. Also there is a dog and I just maybe sighed so hard I caused my poor cat's fur to ruffle. Aside: Not my fault she likes to get close when I am reading. Tick Tock actually shows that Koontz has a sense of humor. There are parts of this that are funny though when you find out the why behind this mess you are going to shake your head. <br /><br />"Tick Tock" has Tommy Phan on the run for his life. Tommy is a successful writer who is dealing with his mother's constant disappointment that he is not a traditional Vietnamese son. Due to his success she is upset that Tommy has forgotten where he has come from. Tommy comes home and finds a rag doll on his steps and stupidly decides to bring it inside with him. When the doll turns into something monstrous, Tommy finds himself on the run from it along with a weird woman named Deliverance who seems to know more than she is letting on and her dog she calls Scottie. If Tommy can live til dawn, the rag doll monster thing won't be able to hurt him. <br /><br />I felt bad for Tommy. I used to get those phone calls from relatives telling me how I forgot about them and now that I am all successful I don't come home anymore. Bah. Tommy pushing back against his mother by eating a cheeseburger was hilarious.<br /><br />Tommy is worried about Deliverance (Del), but they are both really funny together. I didn't guess Deliverance's secret, and I doubt readers coming into this cold will either. It really does come out of nowhere and you are going to love it. Deliverance is very much a kick ass female heroine in this one. I think many of the reasons it didn't bother me in this book was because everything is being played for laughs. I started to chuckle and outright laughed several times while reading this one. <br /><br />The writing was really good and I think that this may be the first and maybe last Koontz novel that featured a POC. I really wish that Koontz had followed up on this one, or even put out more lighter fare. This one is not bogged down by being overly descriptive and off the wall like later Koontz books. You are dealing with a horror book with fantasy elements in it and things tie together nicely. <br /><br />The ending was pretty brilliant and also funny as hell. I don't want to say too much cause just a little bit will spoil you. <br /><br />One of the main reasons why I didn't give this five stars, Tommy should have put two and two together a lot quicker to realize what was going on. Really again with the dog thing Koontz? </span>
  <a data-text-id="16652678196420518064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421920638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421920638" />
    <a title="Janie Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson"><img alt="Janie Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486148700p2/5116650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421920638?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janie Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janie Johnson" href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson">Janie Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer3955258376899032809">In the beginning, the first 25 pages or so, the book seemed to be a little wordy, a little draggy, and then boom you enter a world of doom with a creepy little white demon doll! Chapter 2 was definitely the highlight of the book for me.<br/><br/>I thought it was pretty cool how Tommy compared himself to his detective character in his book. He was the complete opposite of him, but you could tell he wanted to be like him. He had a great character in the story, but I would have liked to see him become a stro</span>
  <span id="freeText3955258376899032809" style="display:none">In the beginning, the first 25 pages or so, the book seemed to be a little wordy, a little draggy, and then boom you enter a world of doom with a creepy little white demon doll! Chapter 2 was definitely the highlight of the book for me.<br /><br />I thought it was pretty cool how Tommy compared himself to his detective character in his book. He was the complete opposite of him, but you could tell he wanted to be like him. He had a great character in the story, but I would have liked to see him become a stronger character.<br /><br />I also like Del a lot too. I loved the air of mystery that surrounded her and her family, including the dog. I think the 'humorous' aspect of the book took away from the whole 'creepy' premise of the story though. It scary/creepy just kinda disappeared. So that was disappointing for me. It went from 'edge of my seat' straight to comedy club material. I also was disappointed with the ending of the story as well. Not what I expected at all.<br /> <br />Overall it is a pretty entertaining book. Fast and easy to read and follow. But because I feel like it was not what it could have been. I gave it 3.5 stars.</span>

    <a title="Todd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/807099-todd"><img alt="Todd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200883115p2/807099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/47171857?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Todd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Todd" href="/user/show/807099-todd">Todd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553582925" href="/book/show/339511.Ticktock">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47171857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10536752997461770828">Dean Koontz created a real page turner in TICK TOCK. Heck, even the cover art works well with the book on this one. It's an all around winner. I'll tell you up front one complaint that keeps it from being a 5 star - it's only one book.<br/><br/>The book chronicles the night from hell for Tommy Phan. Starting with the purchase of his first corvette the ride just keeps going from there.<br/><br/>This book is not what it seems at first. When I picked this up I expected a horror story, with focus on Tommy and a demonic</span>
  <span id="freeText10536752997461770828" style="display:none">Dean Koontz created a real page turner in TICK TOCK. Heck, even the cover art works well with the book on this one. It's an all around winner. I'll tell you up front one complaint that keeps it from being a 5 star - it's only one book.<br /><br />The book chronicles the night from hell for Tommy Phan. Starting with the purchase of his first corvette the ride just keeps going from there.<br /><br />This book is not what it seems at first. When I picked this up I expected a horror story, with focus on Tommy and a demonic pursuer. I was set up for one scare after the next as Tommy is chased and tormented.<br /><br />It was so much more than that. This is drama, horror, and love story rolled into one. It's a story about social moors, tradition, and family as well.<br /><br />Tommy is forced to confront his past and traditions. Along the way he hooks up with Del, a woman with a unique family and history. The demon thing gives chase at first to just Tommy but soon it's chasing them both across the city and beyond.<br /><br />Make no mistake, there are chilling demon tormenting moments, scary monster eating innocent scenes, and relentless pursuit. But just the same, there is a bit of magic, a few wild car rides, and a trip to Las Vegas.<br /><br />All that's missing from this story is Elvis.<br /><br />The title implies something to do with a ticking clock or computer countdown. Oh, there's a countdown the computer and clock having nothing to do with the story. That's my other gripe. Though the story takes place all in about 18 hours, the count down isn't shown on clock, computer, or really even a watch.<br /><br />If you like Koontz, you'll enjoy this. It's quirky, scary and fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10536752997461770828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1088082562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088082562" />
    <a title="Jim C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c"><img alt="Jim C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340034171p2/10296231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1088082562?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1088082562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14808709573198993461">Another supernatural story from Dean Koontz. In this novel, Tommy hails from a traditional Vietnamese family but he has become Americanized. His mother doesn't approve of his ways. Without knowing why he is thrust into a supernatural nightmare. If he can live to see the next dawn he will survive this nightmare.<br/><br/>This one was a reread for me. When it first came out I thought it was okay but this time I enjoyed it so much. If you have read this author's books you will recognize all his trademarks li</span>
  <span id="freeText14808709573198993461" style="display:none">Another supernatural story from Dean Koontz. In this novel, Tommy hails from a traditional Vietnamese family but he has become Americanized. His mother doesn't approve of his ways. Without knowing why he is thrust into a supernatural nightmare. If he can live to see the next dawn he will survive this nightmare.<br /><br />This one was a reread for me. When it first came out I thought it was okay but this time I enjoyed it so much. If you have read this author's books you will recognize all his trademarks like the chase between evil and good, the enigmatic woman, and of course the intelligent dog. This novel isn't as scary as his other works because he added humor to the mix and at times I did giggle out loud. The main character isn't the most memorable character but his supporting cast was terrific and getting to know them was a pure delight. The difference between the characters was a nice display of contrast. <br /><br />This is a short quick read. I know that people have said Koontz isn't the same writer he once was. This book is one of his earlier works and harkens back to the way he did write novels. Fans of Koontz will enjoy this novel and also fall in love with the dog Scootie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14808709573198993461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1085585454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9254376142346543718">A good suspense thriller/chase book as the main characters try to escape "TickTock" the "Deadline to Dawn". The main characters are Vietnamese. Tommy Phan finds a straw/rag doll with stitches on heart/eyes on his step. When the stitches popped off the doll turns into a devil but they try to get the stitches back onto </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124909119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15337522654399815907">I’m not sure when I first read this novel in paperback form, but it was probably right around the time it hit the shelves for sale in 1996. I adored it then, and it remained one of my favorite Koontz novels for a very long time. <br/>I thought I would reread it again for the first time since maybe 2000, but this time listen to it in audiobook form. To maybe see if it stood the test of time, and if I loved it just as much. And while I’m not quite so adoring of this novel now, as I see it’s flaws and s</span>
  <span id="freeText15337522654399815907" style="display:none">I’m not sure when I first read this novel in paperback form, but it was probably right around the time it hit the shelves for sale in 1996. I adored it then, and it remained one of my favorite Koontz novels for a very long time. <br />I thought I would reread it again for the first time since maybe 2000, but this time listen to it in audiobook form. To maybe see if it stood the test of time, and if I loved it just as much. And while I’m not quite so adoring of this novel now, as I see it’s flaws and silliness, I still enjoyed it throughout the audiobook’s length. <br />Koontz insists this novel is patterned after a “screwball comedy” like the old b&amp;w movies ‘Bringing Up Baby’, etc. I don’t think the novel (or audiobook) made it to this level of comedy, screwball or not. I’m a HUGE fan of old black and white movies, and the movies Koontz compares this novel to are some of my all time favorites, which I’ve watched repeatedly. (Mainly because of my enduring love for Carey Grant). This novel just isn’t as good, I’m sorry to say. I don’t know if it’s because I’ve grown a lot since reading this novel when it first came out, or because my taste in novels has changed a good deal since then. But it’s not the same.<br />Paul Michael is the narrator, and he did a pretty good variation of many male and female Vietnamese accents, pretty well. <br />The first time I scored this novel on goodreads back when I added a ton of novels I’d read before, but could not remember exactly when, I’d given this novel 4 stars. I think I should change this to 3.5 stars now. I’d have scored it a solid 3, but I liked the HEA ending, even though I don’t really root for, insist on, or even like HEA endings. It was just fitting, here in this novel.<br />Anyway, read it if you want to. I’m not your mom, and you can do what you want to. 😝</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2107359464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107359464" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steff" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steff" href="/user/show/20701296-steff">Steff</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345533456" href="/book/show/13154941-ticktock">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">genre mixers </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20701296-steff?shelf=what-the-hell">what-the-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20701296-steff?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20701296-steff?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20701296-steff?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20701296-steff?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20701296-steff?shelf=read-at-work">read-at-work</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20701296-steff?shelf=horror-junky">horror-junky</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107359464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9981433318410508032">First initial thought after finishing this "what the hell just happened". This book started off good! I was totally into it and then, then Del Payne came upon the scene. <br/><br/><b>"You're a total fruitcake, Del" </b><br/><br/>That quote not only describes the character of Deliverance "Del" Payne but also acurately describes the book. <br/><br/>The book started off promising Tommy Phan is a likable character with problems that any reader could probably connect with. The horror (I guess you'd call them horror) parts of the book we</span>
  <span id="freeText9981433318410508032" style="display:none">First initial thought after finishing this "what the hell just happened". This book started off good! I was totally into it and then, then Del Payne came upon the scene. <br /><br /><b>"You're a total fruitcake, Del" </b><br /><br />That quote not only describes the character of Deliverance "Del" Payne but also acurately describes the book. <br /><br />The book started off promising Tommy Phan is a likable character with problems that any reader could probably connect with. The horror (I guess you'd call them horror) parts of the book were well written and kept me turning the pages. The devil doll was a good monster to be running from, it's unstoppable and is evolving. I really enjoyed the beginning of the book up until Del comes in. Even awhile after Del came in I could deal with her character. But there was a point where I could take no more. I kept reading and enjoyed other parts of the book. <br /><br />In the afterword by Koontz he said he wanted to write something light and mixed horror with screwball comedy. I understand why he'd want to write something light and don't hold that against him. The mixing of the two just didn't sit well with me, that's not what I was after when I decided to read this book. I didn't want comedy and horror mixed. This reminded me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5931576.Monster" title="Monster by A. Lee Martinez" rel="nofollow noopener">Monster</a> by A. Lee Martinez, I didn't like that one either. <br /><br />So potential readers keep that in mind when regarding my review. If that is what you are looking for I'd suggest this book to you. But if you're looking for the monster of the week type book skip this one unless you want a touch of as Dean calls it "screwball comedy". Overall I'd give this a 2.5 out of 5 stars, 2.5 for the horror scenes and for some of the characters basically all the characters except Del. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9981433318410508032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5750362563927030772">When I first joined Goodreads, I had about a good 20 minutes of fun searching books that I had read and giving them ratings based off of memory. Tick Tock was a book I had read like 15 years ago and I had recalled enjoying it a lot so I gave it five stars.   <span id="freeText5750362563927030772" style="display:none">When I first joined Goodreads, I had about a good 20 minutes of fun searching books that I had read and giving them ratings based off of memory. Tick Tock was a book I had read like 15 years ago and I had recalled enjoying it a lot so I gave it five stars. I remember there being a doll that morphs into a monster that chases the main character around and my memory seemed to recall that it was one of the best Koontz books I'd read at the time. <br /><br />So now I read it again. I was excited to do so. The first 50 or so pages read exactly how I had remembered them. Then the book got bad. I didn't remember that. Once Del gets introduced the book gets annoying fast. It goes from scary to ridiculous with the majority of the second half of the book being stupid conversation (that I imagine Koontz thought was witty and hilarious) and the "creature" ends up being a big joke by the end. I also want to take a second to complain about the dog in this book. Why...oh why...does Dean Koontz have to have some ridiculous, heroic dog in every other book I read of his. <br /><br />I hate dogs.<br /><br />My entire family is allergic to them. They lick their own butts. Poop in the yard. Get put on a higher pedestal than humans by many people. Sorry...I just can't stand the filthy animals. (Except your dog of course. I'm sure I'd love your dog) Koontz loves em though and I guess I should just accept that if I'm going to continue reading more of his work. <br /><br />(To all the dog lovers reading this..if anyone at all even reads this...I apologize for venting)<br /><br />All in all, I changed my rating from five stars to two stars. It earns two stars for reminding me somewhat of the movie Jeepers Creepers. I love that movie. Think I'll watch it again and forget I even reread this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5750362563927030772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney Hoover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney Hoover" href="/user/show/10557432-courtney-hoover">Courtney Hoover</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer359747143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6275812268775875589">This is one of Koontz's more fun, adventurous, pulse-ounding books with lots of unexpected twists and turns to it. As I was reading it, I kept calling it an 'odd book but pretty good,' which is still how I feel about it for the most part. It's a mixture of sci-fi and horror but always with some levity in it and a great Koontz adventure that will leave you breathless with an added element of humor and just a bit of romance. There's an interesting "Note to the reader" at the end of the book that s</span>
  <span id="freeText6275812268775875589" style="display:none">This is one of Koontz's more fun, adventurous, pulse-ounding books with lots of unexpected twists and turns to it. As I was reading it, I kept calling it an 'odd book but pretty good,' which is still how I feel about it for the most part. It's a mixture of sci-fi and horror but always with some levity in it and a great Koontz adventure that will leave you breathless with an added element of humor and just a bit of romance. There's an interesting "Note to the reader" at the end of the book that says that he had previously written several very heavy, dark stories to this one and he felt the need to lighten the mood, both for himself and for his readers, which produced this book. He was successful in his quest if you ask me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6275812268775875589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uOVw7HTr+IGpd5mfyqc/uq/LaDwhNUQsGYFmR4Zj8uc1Ox74eSOyAUsPcIAH3KFSKZTEPb72ucxAghjUxRbUug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

He makes a handsome living doing what he enjoys. His wife, Penny, a children\'s book author and illustrator, is the love of his life. Together they have a brilliant six-year-old, Milo, affectionately dubbed &quot;Spooky,&quot; and a non-collie named Lassie, who\'s all but part of the family.\n\nSo Cubby knows he shouldn\'t let one bad review of his otherwise triumphant new book get to him — even if it does appear in the nation\'s premier newspaper and is penned by the much-feared, seldom-seen critic Shearman Waxx. Cubby knows that the best thing to do is ignore the gratuitously vicious, insulting, and inaccurate comments. Penny knows it; even little Milo knows it. If Lassie could talk, she\'d tell Cubby to ignore them, too.\n\nIgnore Shearman Waxx and his poison pen is just what Cubby intends to do. It\'s a world Jeff Converse, a young<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3898729647763036\" style=\"display:none\">In Manhattan Hunt Club John Saul plumbs the depths of the Manhattan underground--the network of subway tunnels and secret caverns and chambers where the homeless denizens of the city have created their own society. It\'s a world Jeff Converse, a young college student convicted of a crime he didn\'t commit, never knew existed until he is plunged into it after an &quot;accident&quot; that occurs while he is being transported to prison. He soon realizes that it\'s no accident, but the opening move in a deadly game being played by some of the city\'s most powerful men and women, a game in which he is the prey and they are the hunters. Jeff\'s only chance to make it to the surface and survive lies in allying himself with a homicidal maniac who\'s appointed himself the young man\'s protector, but whose designs on Jeff are almost as lethal as those of his enemies in the Manhattan Hunt Club. Saul made his reputation in the horror genre, but he now focuses on psychological terrors rather than things that go bump in the night. His narrative gifts are displayed to great advantage in this heart-stopping thriller; the pacing is flawless and the central characters are very well developed. What keeps this from living up to its fullest potential is the inadequate motivation of the villains, who are largely one-dimensional cardboard cutouts. But that won\'t keep this otherwise topnotch thriller off the bestseller lists, where Saul (Nightshade, The Right Hand of Evil), like Stephen King, is a perennial contender for the number one spot.
